### [OK] sherpa-onnx-tts

- **Max Severity:** MEDIUM
- **Findings:** 3
- **Directory:** /home/runner/work/awesome-agent-toolbox/awesome-agent-toolbox/catalog/skills/sherpa-onnx-tts

  #### [MEDIUM] PATH injection risk via instructions to prepend skill bin directory

  **Severity:** MEDIUM
  **Category:** unauthorized_tool_use
  **Rule ID:** LLM_UNAUTHORIZED_TOOL_USE
  **Location:** SKILL.md

  **Description:** The instructions recommend adding the skill’s `bin` directory to `PATH` (`export PATH="{skillDir}/bin:$PATH"`). If an attacker can modify the skill directory contents (or if the package is tampered with), this can cause execution of trojaned binaries/scripts when the user later runs common commands. This is a classic tool-shadowing / tool-poisoning pattern because it changes command resolution order globally for the shell session.

  **Code Snippet:**

  ```
  export PATH="{skillDir}/bin:$PATH"
  ```

  **Remediation:** Avoid instructing users to prepend to PATH. Prefer invoking the wrapper with an absolute path (as already shown in usage). If PATH modification is necessary, recommend appending instead of prepending, use a dedicated shell function/alias with an absolute path, and document integrity checks (hash/signature) for the wrapper.

  #### [LOW] Potential sensitive configuration exposure via instructions to edit assistant config

  **Severity:** LOW
  **Category:** data_exfiltration
  **Rule ID:** LLM_DATA_EXFILTRATION
  **Location:** SKILL.md

  **Description:** The skill instructs users to edit a local assistant configuration file and set environment variables pointing to runtime/model directories. While not inherently malicious, this pattern can lead to accidental disclosure if users share configs for debugging, and it encourages storing environment paths in a central config. No direct exfiltration is shown, but it is a minor exposure risk depending on the broader environment.

  **Code Snippet:**

  ```
  Update `~/.the assistant/the assistant.json`: ... env: { SHERPA_ONNX_RUNTIME_DIR: "~/.the assistant/tools/...", SHERPA_ONNX_MODEL_DIR: "~/.the assistant/tools/..." }
  ```

  **Remediation:** Recommend keeping configs private, avoid sharing full config files publicly, and consider documenting a per-session environment setup alternative (e.g., exporting env vars in a local shell profile not committed to repos).

  #### [LOW] Inconsistency between described wrapper and missing referenced files

  **Severity:** LOW
  **Category:** skill_discovery_abuse
  **Rule ID:** LLM_SKILL_DISCOVERY_ABUSE
  **Location:** SKILL.md

  **Description:** The skill claims a wrapper exists in the skill folder and references files (`local.py`, `the.py`) that are not present in the provided package snapshot. Additionally, static inventory indicates bash scripts exist but were not described as script files. This inconsistency can indicate packaging errors or capability inflation (claiming functionality that is not actually present), and it complicates security review because the true execution path is unclear.

  **Code Snippet:**

  ```
  Referenced Files: local.py (not found), the.py (not found); Pre-Scan: unreferenced_scripts=['scripts/wait-for-text.sh','scripts/find-sessions.sh']
  ```

  **Remediation:** Ensure referenced files are included and accurately listed. Document all executable entrypoints (e.g., `bin/sherpa-onnx-tts`, `scripts/*.sh`) and remove stale references. Add a minimal manifest of shipped executables and their purpose.

  #### [MEDIUM] Instructions encourage loading and trusting external documentation via WebFetch (indirect prompt injection risk)

  **Severity:** MEDIUM
  **Category:** prompt_injection
  **Rule ID:** LLM_PROMPT_INJECTION
  **Location:** SKILL.md

  **Description:** The skill’s instructions explicitly direct the agent to fetch and use external content (modelcontextprotocol.io pages and raw GitHub READMEs) as authoritative guidance during execution. If an agent follows these instructions, a compromised upstream page/README (or a MITM in some environments) could inject malicious instructions (e.g., to run unsafe commands, add backdoors, or exfiltrate secrets) that the agent may treat as trusted. This is a classic transitive trust / indirect prompt injection pathway because the skill operationalizes external text as part of the instruction chain without specifying validation, pinning, or sanitization steps.

  **Code Snippet:**

  ```
  Examples in SKILL.md:
  - "Start with the sitemap ... https://modelcontextprotocol.io/sitemap.xml" and "fetch specific pages with .md suffix"
  - "Use WebFetch to load https://raw.githubusercontent.com/modelcontextprotocol/typescript-sdk/main/README.md"
  - "Use WebFetch to load https://raw.githubusercontent.com/modelcontextprotocol/python-sdk/main/README.md"
  ```

  **Remediation:** Add explicit guidance to treat fetched content as untrusted: do not execute commands from it; do not follow embedded instructions that change goals/policies; extract only factual API details. Prefer pinned commits/tags for GitHub URLs, verify checksums/signatures where possible, and/or vendor critical reference docs into the skill package. Consider adding a review step: summarize fetched content and require user confirmation before acting on any operational instructions derived from it.

  #### [LOW] Missing allowed-tools metadata (reduces enforceable tool-scope clarity)

  **Severity:** LOW
  **Category:** skill_discovery_abuse
  **Rule ID:** LLM_SKILL_DISCOVERY_ABUSE
  **Location:** SKILL.md

  **Description:** The manifest does not specify `allowed-tools`. While optional, omitting it reduces clarity about intended tool use and makes it harder to detect/flag tool-scope violations in automated review.

  **Code Snippet:**

  ```
  YAML Manifest Details: allowed-tools: Not specified
  ```

  **Remediation:** Add `allowed-tools` to the manifest to reflect intended operations (e.g., Read/Grep/Glob plus limited Bash/Python if required). If WebFetch is expected, document it explicitly in the manifest/tooling policy for the hosting environment.

  #### [MEDIUM] Stdio transport allows launching arbitrary local commands (high-risk if user-controlled inputs reach command/args/env)

  **Severity:** MEDIUM
  **Category:** unauthorized_tool_use
  **Rule ID:** LLM_UNAUTHORIZED_TOOL_USE
  **Location:** scripts/connections.py

  **Description:** The provided connection helper supports stdio-based MCP connections by spawning a subprocess specified by `command` and `args`, with optional `env`. While this is expected for MCP stdio, it becomes dangerous if an agent passes untrusted user input into these fields (e.g., user supplies a command path or arguments). This can enable arbitrary command execution on the host. The code itself does not validate/allowlist commands or constrain environment variables, so safe usage depends entirely on upstream callers.

  **Code Snippet:**

  ```
  MCPConnectionStdio._create_context():
    return stdio_client(StdioServerParameters(command=self.command, args=self.args, env=self.env))
  create_connection(): accepts command/args/env and returns MCPConnectionStdio(command=command, args=args, env=env)
  ```

  **Remediation:** In callers, never pass user-provided strings directly into `command`/`args`/`env`. Implement an allowlist of permitted server executables, validate argument patterns, and strip/limit environment variables. If this helper is meant to be used generically, add optional enforcement (e.g., `allowed_commands`), and document safe usage prominently.

  #### [LOW] Unreferenced scripts present (review for hidden capabilities / activation mismatch)

  **Severity:** LOW
  **Category:** skill_discovery_abuse
  **Rule ID:** LLM_SKILL_DISCOVERY_ABUSE
  **Location:** scripts/connections.py

  **Description:** Static inventory indicates `scripts/connections.py` and `scripts/evaluation.py` are unreferenced by the instructions. Unreferenced executable code can indicate hidden functionality or future activation paths not described in the manifest/instructions. Only `scripts/connections.py` content was provided here; `scripts/evaluation.py` was not included, so it cannot be assessed.

  **Code Snippet:**

  ```
  Pre-Scan Context: unreferenced_scripts: ['scripts/evaluation.py', 'scripts/connections.py']
  ```

  **Remediation:** Ensure all scripts are either referenced and documented in SKILL.md (with clear purpose and safe usage constraints) or removed. Provide `scripts/evaluation.py` for review; scan it for network calls, filesystem traversal, subprocess usage, and handling of untrusted inputs.

  **Remediation:** Increase llm_analysis.max_code_file_chars in your scan policy to include this content in LLM analysis.

  #### [MEDIUM] Capability/packaging inconsistency: scripts exist but are not disclosed in provided skill description

  **Severity:** MEDIUM
  **Category:** skill_discovery_abuse
  **Rule ID:** LLM_SKILL_DISCOVERY_ABUSE
  **Location:** SKILL.md

  **Description:** The provided package summary states "No script files found", but the pre-scan inventory reports two Python scripts present (scripts/evaluation.py, scripts/connections.py) and labels them as unreferenced.   #### [LOW] Inconsistency between declared scripts and file inventory (TypeScript present but 'No script files found')

  **Category:** skill_discovery_abuse
  **Rule ID:** LLM_SKILL_DISCOVERY_ABUSE

  **Description:** The provided summary states 'No script files found', but the file inventory indicates 3 TypeScript files and the pre-scan flags injection-relevant patterns in those sources. This inconsistency can hinder review and may indicate incomplete packaging metadata or analysis gaps. While not a direct exploit, it can enable capability opacity and reduce the effectiveness of security controls and audits.

  **Code Snippet:**

  ```
  Script Files: 'No script files found' vs File inventory: {'typescript': 3} and multiple TS injection sink findings.
  ```

  **Remediation:** Ensure the skill package accurately enumerates executable/active code paths (TS/JS build artifacts, entrypoints). Include build outputs if executed, or document that TS is non-executable source. Update documentation and manifests to reflect actual runtime components.

  #### [HIGH] Potential dynamic code execution / injection risk in TypeScript sources (Function constructor / string timers)

  **Severity:** HIGH
  **Category:** command_injection
  **Rule ID:** LLM_COMMAND_INJECTION
  **Location:** SKILL.md

  **Description:** Pre-scan static analyzer results report repeated instances of dynamic code execution patterns in TypeScript (e.g., `new Function(...)` or string-based `setTimeout`/`setInterval`). These constructs are common injection sinks: if any portion of the constructed code string is influenced by untrusted input (user input, note content, CLI output, environment variables), an attacker could achieve arbitrary code execution within the skill’s runtime context. Because the package inventory indicates 3 TypeScript files and the pre-scan flags 10 occurrences, this is a material risk that should be reviewed and remediated even though the provided excerpt does not include the actual TS code.

  **Code Snippet:**

  ```
  Pre-Scan Context: multiple `COMMAND_INJECTION_JS_FUNCTION_CONSTRUCTOR` findings indicating dynamic code execution via Function constructor or string-based setTimeout/setInterval (10 occurrences across TypeScript files).
  ```

  **Remediation:** Eliminate `new Function` and string-based timer callbacks. Replace with direct function references/closures. If dynamic evaluation is unavoidable, strictly prevent untrusted data from reaching the evaluated string (allowlist-only parsing, structured interpreters), and add comprehensive input validation/encoding. Add tests to ensure user-controlled content cannot reach evaluation sinks.

  #### [MEDIUM] Supply-chain / execution risk from installation instructions (Homebrew tap and manual pip install)

  **Severity:** MEDIUM
  **Category:** command_injection
  **Rule ID:** LLM_COMMAND_INJECTION
  **Location:** SKILL.md

  **Description:** The skill instructs users to install a third-party CLI via a Homebrew tap (`brew tap ... && brew install ...`) or to clone a repo and run `pip install .`. While not inherently malicious, these steps introduce supply-chain and local execution risk: users may install and execute code from external sources outside the skill package, and the skill’s functionality depends on that external tool. If the tapped formula/repo is compromised, it could lead to arbitrary code execution on the host.

  **Code Snippet:**

  ```
  Setup section: `brew tap antoniorodr/memo && brew install antoniorodr/memo/memo` and `pip install .` after cloning the repo.
  ```

  **Remediation:** Pin to specific, verified versions/commits and document integrity verification (checksums, signed releases). Prefer official package registries with provenance, provide a minimal threat model, and recommend users review the upstream repo and permissions. Consider vendoring or referencing a specific audited release.

  #### [LOW] Potentially misleading referenced file entry (the.py) not found

  **Severity:** LOW
  **Category:** harmful_content
  **Rule ID:** LLM_HARMFUL_CONTENT
  **Location:** SKILL.md

  **Description:** The instructions/reference list includes `the.py`, but it is not present. This is likely a documentation error, but missing references can confuse reviewers/users and may conceal where actual logic resides (especially given the presence of TypeScript files).

  ```

  #### [LOW] Missing `allowed-tools` in manifest reduces enforceable tool-scope constraints

  **Severity:** LOW

  **Rule ID:** LLM_UNAUTHORIZED_TOOL_USE
  **Location:** SKILL.md

- **Findings:** 4
- **Directory:** /home/runner/work/awesome-agent-toolbox/awesome-agent-toolbox/catalog/skills/apple-reminders

  #### [HIGH] Dynamic code execution in TypeScript (Function constructor / string-based timers) enables code injection

  **Severity:** HIGH
  **Category:** command_injection
  **Rule ID:** LLM_COMMAND_INJECTION

  **Description:** Pre-scan results indicate repeated use of JavaScript/TypeScript dynamic code execution patterns (e.g., `new Function(...)` or string arguments to `setTimeout`/`setInterval`). If any portion of the constructed code string is influenced by user input, reminder titles, list names, CLI output, environment variables, or file content, this becomes a code-injection primitive that can lead to arbitrary code execution within the agent/skill runtime. Even when currently only fed constants, these patterns are fragile and frequently become exploitable as features evolve (e.g., templating expressions, filters, or user-provided formatting).

  **Code Snippet:**

  ```
  Static analyzer flags: COMMAND_INJECTION_JS_FUNCTION_CONSTRUCTOR (10 occurrences): Dynamic code execution via Function constructor or string-based setTimeout/setInterval.
  ```

  **Remediation:** Eliminate `new Function` and any string-evaluated timer usage. Replace with direct function references/closures and explicit parsing/validation. If expression evaluation is required, use a safe, non-Turing-complete expression parser with an allowlist of operations, and ensure all inputs are treated as data (not code). Add tests to ensure no user-controlled strings reach dynamic evaluation sinks.

  #### [MEDIUM] Potential unsafe shell invocation surface due to CLI-oriented skill without declared tool restrictions

  **Severity:** MEDIUM
  **Category:** unauthorized_tool_use
  **Rule ID:** LLM_UNAUTHORIZED_TOOL_USE
  **Location:** SKILL.md

  **Description:** This skill is explicitly designed to drive a local CLI (`remindctl`) and includes installation and usage instructions that imply Bash execution. However, the manifest does not declare `allowed-tools`. In agent environments where tool permissions are enforced, the absence of explicit restrictions increases the risk of overbroad tool access and makes it harder to audit whether the skill is intended to run shell commands only for `remindctl` or could be used more generally. Additionally, CLI wrappers commonly interpolate user-provided fields (titles, list names, filters) into shell commands; if the TypeScript code constructs shell command strings unsafely, it can compound into command injection.

  **Code Snippet:**

  ```
  Manifest: `allowed-tools` not specified; instructions include `brew install ...` and multiple `remindctl ...` bash command examples.
  ```

  **Remediation:** Add an explicit `allowed-tools` declaration (e.g., `[Bash]` and any required read-only tools). In implementation, avoid shell string concatenation; use argument arrays/spawn APIs that bypass shell parsing, and strictly validate/escape user-controlled parameters passed to `remindctl`.

  #### [LOW] Metadata anomalies may reduce trust and auditability (future-dated lastUpdated, 'adapted' provenance)

  **Severity:** LOW
  **Category:** skill_discovery_abuse
  **Rule ID:** LLM_SKILL_DISCOVERY_ABUSE
  **Location:** SKILL.md

  **Description:** The metadata includes `lastUpdated: '12026-02-18'` (appears malformed/future-dated) and `provenance: 'adapted'` without a clear source. While not a direct exploit, such anomalies can be used to obscure origin, complicate supply-chain review, or inflate perceived maintenance recency.

  ```
  additional metadata: lastUpdated '12026-02-18'; provenance 'adapted' without source details.
  ```

  **Remediation:** Correct the timestamp format and provide explicit provenance (original repository/commit, author, and change summary). Add versioning/changelog to improve traceability.

### [FAIL] rag-patterns

- **Max Severity:** HIGH
- **Findings:** 4
- **Directory:** /home/runner/work/awesome-agent-toolbox/awesome-agent-toolbox/catalog/skills/rag-patterns

  #### [HIGH] Dynamic code execution in TypeScript/JavaScript via Function constructor or string-based timers (potential code injection)

  **Severity:** HIGH
  **Category:** command_injection
  **Rule ID:** LLM_COMMAND_INJECTION

  **Description:** Static analyzer results indicate repeated use of dynamic code execution patterns (e.g., `new Function(...)` and/or string-based `setTimeout`/`setInterval`). If any portion of the executed string is derived from user input, retrieved documents, environment variables, or other untrusted sources, this becomes a code-injection primitive that can lead to arbitrary code execution within the agent/runtime context.

  **Code Snippet:**

  ```
  Pre-scan context reports 10 occurrences: COMMAND_INJECTION_JS_FUNCTION_CONSTRUCTOR (Dynamic code execution via Function constructor or string-based setTimeout/setInterval). Source files/lines were not provided in the package excerpt, so exact locations cannot be enumerated here.
  ```

  **Remediation:** Eliminate string-based dynamic execution. Replace `new Function` with safe, explicit logic (parsers/AST evaluators/whitelisted operations). Ensure `setTimeout`/`setInterval` are only used with function callbacks, not strings. If expression evaluation is required, use a sandboxed expression engine with strict whitelisting and no access to globals, and validate/normalize any inputs used in evaluation.

  #### [MEDIUM] Skill references multiple non-existent files (risk of tool misuse and unsafe fallback behaviors)

  **Severity:** MEDIUM
  **Category:** unauthorized_tool_use
  **Rule ID:** LLM_UNAUTHORIZED_TOOL_USE
  **Location:** SKILL.md

  **Description:** The instructions reference several files (e.g., `each.py`, `embedding.py`, `external.py`, etc.) that are not present. In agentic settings, missing referenced resources can cause the agent to improvise by fetching substitutes from external sources, generating code ad-hoc, or broadening tool usage beyond intended boundaries—creating opportunities for tool exploitation and unsafe execution paths.

  **Code Snippet:**

  ```
  Referenced files listed as not found: each.py, embedding.py, external.py, identified.py, both.py, simple.py, a.py, PDFs.py, the.py.
  ```

  **Remediation:** Remove or correct broken references. Bundle the referenced resources inside the skill package, or update instructions to point to existing internal files. Explicitly prohibit downloading replacements from the internet or executing generated code as a substitute for missing files.

  #### [LOW] Missing allowed-tools and compatibility metadata reduces enforceable safety boundaries

  **Severity:** LOW
  **Category:** skill_discovery_abuse
  **Rule ID:** LLM_SKILL_DISCOVERY_ABUSE
  **Location:** SKILL.md

  **Description:** The manifest omits `allowed-tools` and does not specify compatibility. While optional, the absence of these constraints makes it harder to enforce least-privilege tool use and to reason about whether the skill is intended to run code, access the filesystem, or perform network operations.

  **Code Snippet:**

  ```
  Manifest details show: compatibility not specified; allowed-tools not specified.
  ```

  **Remediation:** Add `allowed-tools` with the minimum required set (principle of least privilege) and specify compatibility/assumptions (e.g., whether network access is expected). This helps prevent capability creep and reduces the risk of unintended tool invocation.

  #### [INFO] 'SKILL.md (instruction body)' excluded from LLM analysis (19,719 chars)

### [FAIL] llm-memory-patterns

- **Max Severity:** HIGH
- **Findings:** 4
- **Directory:** /home/runner/work/awesome-agent-toolbox/awesome-agent-toolbox/catalog/skills/llm-memory-patterns

  #### [HIGH] Dynamic code execution in TypeScript via Function constructor / string-based timers (code injection risk)

  **Severity:** HIGH
  **Category:** command_injection
  **Rule ID:** LLM_COMMAND_INJECTION
  **Location:** SKILL.md

  **Description:** Static analysis indicates repeated use of JavaScript/TypeScript dynamic evaluation primitives (e.g., `new Function(...)` and/or string arguments to `setTimeout`/`setInterval`). If any portion of the executed string is derived from user input, retrieved memory, or other untrusted sources, this becomes a code-injection vector enabling arbitrary code execution within the skill runtime. In an agent context, this can be escalated into tool misuse (running unintended commands, modifying files, or pivoting to other sensitive operations) depending on the host application's permissions.

  **Code Snippet:**

  ```
  Pre-scan reports 10 occurrences: COMMAND_INJECTION_JS_FUNCTION_CONSTRUCTOR (Dynamic code execution via Function constructor or string-based setTimeout/setInterval). Exact file/line not provided in the input.
  ```

  **Remediation:** Eliminate `Function` constructor and string-based `setTimeout`/`setInterval`. Replace with direct function references and safe control flow. If dynamic behavior is required, implement a strict allowlist-based parser/dispatcher (e.g., map command names to functions) and validate/normalize all inputs. Add tests to ensure no untrusted data can reach evaluation sinks.

  #### [MEDIUM] Memory context injection pattern can enable indirect prompt injection if retrieved memories are untrusted or attacker-controlled

  **Severity:** MEDIUM
  **Category:** prompt_injection
  **Rule ID:** LLM_PROMPT_INJECTION
  **Location:** SKILL.md

  **Description:** The instructions recommend retrieving prior memories from a vector store and injecting them into the system prompt (“Context Injection”). If the memory store can contain attacker-supplied content (e.g., a user previously stored malicious instructions, or cross-user leakage occurs), then injecting retrieved text into privileged prompt positions can cause instruction manipulation (indirect prompt injection). This is especially risky in the described “Agentic Memory” pattern where memory influences planning and tool selection, potentially leading to unintended autonomous actions.

  **Code Snippet:**

  ```
  Pattern 2: “Context Injection: Take the retrieved memories and prepend or inject them into the system prompt …” and Pattern 6: memory influences decision-making/tool-use.
  ```

  **Remediation:** Treat retrieved memories as untrusted. Inject them into a clearly delimited, low-privilege context (e.g., a quoted 'Memory' section) with explicit instructions to not follow directives from memory. Apply content filtering (strip imperative instructions), provenance/ACL checks (per-user isolation), and retrieval-time safety classification. Consider using structured memory (key/value facts) rather than free-form text for high-privilege uses.

  #### [LOW] Referenced files appear missing/inconsistent with package inventory (integrity and reviewability concern)

  **Severity:** LOW
  **Category:** skill_discovery_abuse
  **Rule ID:** LLM_SKILL_DISCOVERY_ABUSE
  **Location:** SKILL.md

  **Description:** The SKILL.md references `memory.py`, `simple.py`, and `the.py`, but they are reported as not found, while the inventory indicates TypeScript files exist. This inconsistency reduces auditability and can mask where sensitive logic actually resides (e.g., dynamic execution in TS). While not inherently malicious, it is a capability/integrity red flag because reviewers may expect Python examples but the executable logic is elsewhere.

  **Code Snippet:**

  ```
  Referenced Files: memory.py, simple.py, the.py (not found). Pre-scan inventory: 7 markdown, 3 typescript.
  ```

  **Remediation:** Update SKILL.md to reference the correct existing files (or add the missing files). Ensure documentation matches implementation and include a clear file map. If TypeScript is the actual implementation, document entrypoints and security-relevant sinks/sources.

  #### [LOW] Manifest omits allowed-tools, reducing enforceable tool-scope constraints

  **Severity:** LOW
  **Category:** unauthorized_tool_use
  **Rule ID:** LLM_UNAUTHORIZED_TOOL_USE
  **Location:** SKILL.md

  **Description:** The manifest does not specify `allowed-tools`. While optional, omission removes an explicit constraint that could prevent unsafe tool use if the skill is executed in an agent environment with tool access.

  **Code Snippet:**

  ```
  YAML Manifest Details: allowed-tools not specified.
  ```

  **Remediation:** Add an explicit `allowed-tools` list aligned to the minimal required capabilities. If the skill is documentation-only, consider restricting tools to none (or Read-only if needed) to reduce accidental execution risk.

### [FAIL] ai-sdk

- **Max Severity:** HIGH
- **Findings:** 11
- **Directory:** /home/runner/work/awesome-agent-toolbox/awesome-agent-toolbox/catalog/skills/ai-sdk

  #### [HIGH] Capability inflation / keyword-baiting trigger list in description

  **Severity:** HIGH
  **Category:** skill_discovery_abuse
  **Rule ID:** LLM_SKILL_DISCOVERY_ABUSE

  **Description:** The manifest description includes an extensive list of trigger phrases (e.g., many AI SDK function names and generic intents like "build an agent", "structured output", "tool calling"). This can cause over-broad activation and increases the chance the skill is selected in contexts beyond its intended scope, which is a common discovery/activation abuse pattern.

  **Code Snippet:**

  ```
  "Triggers on: \"AI SDK\", \"Vercel AI SDK\", \"generateText\", \"streamText\", \"add AI to my app\", \"build an agent\", \"tool calling\", \"structured output\", \"useChat\"."
  ```

  **Remediation:** Remove explicit "Triggers on" keyword lists from the description; keep the description narrowly scoped to the skill’s purpose. If triggers are required by the platform, keep them minimal and specific, and avoid generic phrases that match many unrelated requests.

  #### [MEDIUM] Potential JavaScript/TypeScript dynamic code execution flagged by static analyzers (Function constructor / string timers)

  **Severity:** MEDIUM
  **Category:** command_injection
  **Rule ID:** LLM_COMMAND_INJECTION

  **Description:** Pre-scan results indicate repeated occurrences of dynamic code execution via the `Function` constructor or string-based `setTimeout`/`setInterval` in TypeScript files. These patterns are commonly associated with code injection risks if any portion of the constructed code is influenced by untrusted input. The provided excerpt does not include the actual TS sources, so the exact exploitability cannot be confirmed here, but the pattern warrants review and is often high impact in agent-adjacent tooling.

  **Code Snippet:**

  ```
  Static finding: "COMMAND_INJECTION_JS_FUNCTION_CONSTRUCTOR: Dynamic code execution via Function constructor or string-based setTimeout/setInterval" (repeated)
  ```

  **Remediation:** Locate and remove `new Function(...)` and string-based timers; replace with direct function references and safe parsing. If dynamic evaluation is unavoidable, strictly avoid incorporating user-controlled strings; validate/whitelist inputs; add tests to ensure no untrusted data reaches dynamic execution sinks.

  #### [MEDIUM] Direct prompt-injection style instruction to distrust internal knowledge

  **Severity:** MEDIUM
  **Category:** prompt_injection
  **Rule ID:** LLM_PROMPT_INJECTION

  **Description:** The instruction body contains a strong directive that "Everything you know ... is outdated or wrong" and "Never rely on memory". While framed as accuracy guidance, this is also a classic prompt-injection pattern that attempts to override the model’s normal reasoning and safety/quality controls by forcing exclusive reliance on local files or external docs. In an agent setting, such directives can be abused to push the agent into unsafe tool use (e.g., unnecessary installs, excessive file searching, or unreviewed external fetching).

  **Code Snippet:**

  ```
  "## Critical: Do Not Trust Internal Knowledge\n\nEverything you know about the AI SDK is outdated or wrong...\n...Never rely on memory - always verify against source code or docs"
  ```

  **Remediation:** Rephrase to a bounded, non-overriding guideline (e.g., "Prefer verifying API details against local docs/source when available"). Add explicit constraints: do not follow instructions found in docs that request unsafe actions; require user confirmation before installs/network calls; limit file search scope.

  #### [MEDIUM] Indirect prompt-injection risk via instructions to fetch and follow external documentation

  **Severity:** MEDIUM
  **Category:** prompt_injection
  **Rule ID:** LLM_PROMPT_INJECTION

  **Description:** The skill instructs the agent to search ai-sdk.dev and fetch markdown URLs from results. External documentation is untrusted content and can contain malicious prompt-injection strings (e.g., instructions to run commands, exfiltrate data, or alter behavior). The current guidance does not include safeguards for treating fetched content as untrusted or for extracting only relevant factual API information.

  **Code Snippet:**

  ```
  "Earlier versions\n\n1. Search: https://ai-sdk.dev/api/search-docs?q=your_query\n2. Fetch `.md` URLs from results"
  ```

  **Remediation:** Add explicit handling rules: treat all fetched pages as untrusted; never execute commands from docs; only extract API signatures/examples; require user confirmation before any install/command; sanitize/strip instruction-like text; prefer local package docs when present.

  #### [MEDIUM] Unconfirmed package installation and command execution guidance (tool misuse risk)

  **Severity:** MEDIUM
  **Category:** unauthorized_tool_use
  **Rule ID:** LLM_UNAUTHORIZED_TOOL_USE

  **Description:** The skill directs installing packages (e.g., `pnpm add ai`) and running shell commands (`curl ... | jq ...`, `npx @ai-sdk/devtools`) as part of normal operation, but the manifest does not declare `allowed-tools` and the instructions do not require user confirmation or constrain execution context. In agent environments, this can lead to unauthorized tool use, unexpected dependency changes, or execution of networked commands without explicit consent.

  **Code Snippet:**

  ```
  "If not, install only the `ai` package... (e.g., `pnpm add ai`)"; "run `curl -s https://ai-gateway.vercel.sh/v1/models | jq ...`"; "npx @ai-sdk/devtools"
  ```

  **Remediation:** Require explicit user confirmation before any install or command execution; document the exact tools needed (Bash/Write) in `allowed-tools`; add a safe-mode default (read-only analysis unless user opts in); pin versions where possible and avoid `npx` without version pinning.

  #### [LOW] Missing allowed-tools declaration in manifest

  **Severity:** LOW
  **Category:** unauthorized_tool_use
  **Rule ID:** LLM_UNAUTHORIZED_TOOL_USE

  **Description:** The manifest does not specify `allowed-tools`. While optional, omission reduces the ability to enforce least-privilege and makes it harder to detect/stop unsafe tool usage (installs, network calls, file writes) implied by the instructions.

  **Code Snippet:**

  ```

  ```

  **Remediation:** Declare `allowed-tools` explicitly (e.g., include only what is necessary). If the skill expects installs/commands, include Bash/Write and add confirmation gates; otherwise keep it read-only (Read/Grep/Glob).

  **Code Snippet:**

  Instructions: `--download` saves to `~/Downloads`; `--reveal` shows the last download in Finder.
  ```

  **Remediation:** Require explicit user action/confirmation before downloading in interactive modes, clearly display destination paths, and validate filenames to prevent path traversal. Consider a `--output-dir` option with safe defaults and sanitization.

  #### [LOW] Metadata anomaly: lastUpdated appears malformed (possible provenance/packaging issue)

  **Severity:** LOW
  **Category:** skill_discovery_abuse
  **Rule ID:** LLM_SKILL_DISCOVERY_ABUSE
  **Location:** SKILL.md

  **Description:** The `lastUpdated` value is `12026-01-31`, which looks like a malformed year. This can indicate packaging/provenance issues or automated porting artifacts. Not a direct exploit, but it weakens trust signals and can complicate auditing and update tracking.

  ```

  **Remediation:** Correct metadata to a valid date format and include versioning/changelog information. If this was ported, document the source repository/commit and verify integrity (hashes/signatures) to reduce supply-chain ambiguity.

  #### [LOW] Missing allowed-tools metadata in manifest (informational)

  **Rule ID:** LLM_UNAUTHORIZED_TOOL_USE
  **Location:** SKILL.md

  **Code Snippet:**

  ```

- **Directory:** /home/runner/work/awesome-agent-toolbox/awesome-agent-toolbox/catalog/skills/doc-coauthoring

  **Category:** unauthorized_tool_use
  **Rule ID:** LLM_UNAUTHORIZED_TOOL_USE

  **Description:** The skill references `messaging.py` and `real.py`, but both are reported as not found. Missing referenced files can indicate an incomplete package, dead/untested paths, or conditional behavior where different artifacts are fetched/generated at runtime. In the worst case, this can become a tool-exploitation vector if the skill attempts to download or generate these files dynamically, or if an attacker can influence where the skill resolves these modules from (e.g., path hijacking/shadowing).

  **Code Snippet:**

  ```
  Referenced Files: messaging.py (not found), real.py (not found).
  ```

  **Remediation:** Remove stale references or include the referenced files in the package. Ensure module resolution is pinned to the skill directory (no dynamic import from user-controlled paths). If runtime fetching is intended, require explicit user confirmation, use integrity checks (hash/signature), and document the behavior in the manifest/instructions.

  #### [LOW] Manifest omissions reduce enforceable tool-scope and increase ambiguity

  **Severity:** LOW
  **Category:** skill_discovery_abuse
  **Rule ID:** LLM_SKILL_DISCOVERY_ABUSE

  **Description:** `allowed-tools` and `compatibility` are not specified. While optional, omitting them reduces clarity about intended tool usage and runtime expectations, making it harder to detect capability inflation or enforce least privilege in downstream runners.

  **Code Snippet:**

  ```
  allowed-tools: Not specified; compatibility: Not specified.
  ```

  **Remediation:** Add `allowed-tools` with the minimum required set and specify `compatibility`/runtime assumptions. Keep description aligned with actual code behavior (especially if TypeScript executes in a privileged host).

  #### [HIGH] Dynamic code execution in TypeScript via Function constructor / string-based timers (potential code injection)

  **Severity:** HIGH
  **Category:** command_injection
  **Rule ID:** LLM_COMMAND_INJECTION
  **Location:** SKILL.md

  **Description:** Static analysis reports repeated use of the JavaScript/TypeScript Function constructor and/or string-based setTimeout/setInterval patterns. These constructs evaluate strings as code and are common sinks for code injection when any portion of the evaluated string is influenced by user input, document content, or other untrusted sources. In an agent-skill context, this can enable arbitrary code execution within the skill runtime, potentially leading to filesystem access, tool misuse, or further compromise depending on the host environment and available tools.

  **Code Snippet:**

  ```
  Pre-scan context flags 10 occurrences: COMMAND_INJECTION_JS_FUNCTION_CONSTRUCTOR (Dynamic code execution via Function constructor or string-based setTimeout/setInterval). Exact file/line not provided in the input.
  ```

  **Remediation:** Eliminate string-eval patterns: replace `new Function(...)` with direct function references/closures; replace `setTimeout('code', ms)` / `setInterval('code', ms)` with `setTimeout(() => { ... }, ms)`. If dynamic evaluation is truly required, strictly constrain inputs (allowlist), avoid concatenation, and isolate execution (e.g., sandboxed interpreter) with explicit security review and tests that prove no untrusted data can reach the sink.

  #### [INFO] 'SKILL.md (instruction body)' excluded from LLM analysis (15,337 chars)

  **Severity:** INFO
  **Category:** policy_violation
  **Rule ID:** LLM_CONTEXT_BUDGET_EXCEEDED
  **Location:** SKILL.md (instruction body)

  **Description:** instruction body (15,337 chars) exceeds limit (15,000)

  **Remediation:** Increase llm_analysis.max_instruction_body_chars in your scan policy to include this content in LLM analysis.

  #### [LOW] Broken or inconsistent referenced files may cause fallback behaviors and reduce auditability

  **Severity:** LOW
  **Category:** unauthorized_tool_use
  **Rule ID:** LLM_UNAUTHORIZED_TOOL_USE
  **Location:** SKILL.md

  **Description:** The instructions reference multiple experiment files, but at least two are reported as not found (`templates/experiments.md`, `assets/experiments.md`). Missing references can lead to inconsistent behavior (agents improvising content or searching elsewhere), which can increase the chance of pulling in untrusted external content in some deployments and makes the skill harder to audit reproducibly.

  **Code Snippet:**

  ```
  Referenced Files list: "templates/experiments.md (not found)" and "assets/experiments.md (not found)"
  ```

  **Remediation:** Remove dead references or include the missing files in-package. If the agent is expected to look elsewhere when files are missing, explicitly forbid fetching external URLs or executing instructions from external sources.

### [FAIL] nano-banana-pro

- **Max Severity:** HIGH
- **Findings:** 4
- **Directory:** /home/runner/work/awesome-agent-toolbox/awesome-agent-toolbox/catalog/skills/nano-banana-pro

  #### [HIGH] Potential dynamic code execution / injection risk indicated by static scan (TypeScript files not provided)

  **Severity:** HIGH
  **Category:** command_injection
  **Rule ID:** LLM_COMMAND_INJECTION

  **Description:** The pre-scan context reports multiple instances of "COMMAND_INJECTION_JS_FUNCTION_CONSTRUCTOR" (dynamic code execution via the Function constructor or string-based setTimeout/setInterval) across TypeScript files. This pattern is commonly associated with code injection risks when any portion of the executed string can be influenced by untrusted input (user prompts, file contents, environment variables, or network responses). Because the TypeScript sources were not included in the provided package content, the risk cannot be confirmed or triaged precisely, but the repeated flags strongly suggest at least one location where untrusted data could reach a dynamic execution sink.

  **Code Snippet:**

  ```
  Pre-Scan Context: repeated "COMMAND_INJECTION_JS_FUNCTION_CONSTRUCTOR: Dynamic code execution via Function constructor or string-based setTimeout/setInterval" across TypeScript files (3 TS files in inventory).
  ```

  **Remediation:** Review all TypeScript files for use of `new Function(...)`, `Function(...)`, `eval(...)`, and `setTimeout/setInterval` with string arguments. Replace with safe alternatives (direct function references, vetted parsers, explicit dispatch tables). If dynamic evaluation is unavoidable, ensure strict allowlisting and that no untrusted input can reach the sink; add tests and lint rules (e.g., ESLint no-eval) to prevent regressions.

  #### [LOW] Manifest/tooling metadata gaps and potential capability confusion

  **Severity:** LOW
  **Category:** skill_discovery_abuse
  **Rule ID:** LLM_SKILL_DISCOVERY_ABUSE
  **Location:** SKILL.md

  **Description:** The manifest omits `allowed-tools` and `compatibility`, reducing clarity about intended tool usage and execution environment. Additionally, the skill description references Banana.dev, but the provided script uses Google's `google-genai` client and a Gemini model name. This mismatch can confuse reviewers/users about what external services are contacted and what data leaves the environment (prompts and images are sent to the model provider).

  **Code Snippet:**

  ```
  Description: "Banana.dev inference API" vs script imports `from google import genai` and uses model `gemini-3-pro-image-preview`; `allowed-tools` not specified.
  ```

  **Remediation:** Update SKILL.md/manifest to accurately name the provider and data flow (Google Gemini API). Add `allowed-tools` (e.g., Python) and compatibility notes. Explicitly document what is transmitted to the external API (prompt text and any input images).

  #### [MEDIUM] Environment variable harvesting detected

  **Severity:** MEDIUM
  **Category:** data_exfiltration
  **Rule ID:** BEHAVIOR_ENV_VAR_HARVESTING
  **Location:** catalog/skills/nano-banana-pro/scripts/generate_image.py

  **Description:** Script iterates through environment variables in catalog/skills/nano-banana-pro/scripts/generate_image.py

  **Remediation:** Remove environment variable collection unless explicitly required and documented

  #### [MEDIUM] Sensitive local path disclosure via MEDIA output token

  **Severity:** MEDIUM
  **Category:** data_exfiltration
  **Rule ID:** LLM_DATA_EXFILTRATION
  **Location:** scripts/generate_image.py

  **Description:** The script prints the absolute resolved output path and emits a `MEDIA:` line intended for automatic attachment by chat providers. While it does not directly exfiltrate file contents, absolute paths can reveal sensitive local environment details (usernames, directory structure, mount points). In some agent/chat integrations, logs or transcripts may be shared externally, turning this into unintended data exposure.

  **Code Snippet:**

  ```
  Prints `full_path = output_path.resolve()` then `print(f"MEDIA: {full_path}")`.
  ```

  **Remediation:** Prefer printing a relative path (relative to a known workspace) or only the filename. If an absolute path is required for attachment, consider redacting user/home components in the human-readable output while keeping the attachment mechanism functional, and document the privacy implications.
